###begin article-title 0
###xml 2 12 2 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 51 56 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">Human</span>
A Drosophila Model for EGFR-Ras and PI3K-Dependent Human Glioma
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Conceived and designed the experiments: RDR WKC FBF JBT. Performed the experiments: RDR. Analyzed the data: RDR WKC FBF JBT. Contributed reagents/materials/analysis tools: RDR WKC FBF JBT. Wrote the paper: RDR JBT. Contributed to study design and data interpretation: RDR WKC FBF JBT. Conceived the project, performed all experiments and image analysis, and wrote the manuscript: RDR. Provided editorial guidance: WKC FBF JBT.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 293 303 293 303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 378 388 378 388 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 598 608 598 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 519 524 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 749 754 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 963 968 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1569 1574 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Gliomas, the most common malignant tumors of the nervous system, frequently harbor mutations that activate the epidermal growth factor receptor (EGFR) and phosphatidylinositol-3 kinase (PI3K) signaling pathways. To investigate the genetic basis of this disease, we developed a glioma model in Drosophila. We found that constitutive coactivation of EGFR-Ras and PI3K pathways in Drosophila glia and glial precursors gives rise to neoplastic, invasive glial cells that create transplantable tumor-like growths, mimicking human glioma. Our model represents a robust organotypic and cell-type-specific Drosophila cancer model in which malignant cells are created by mutations in signature genes and pathways thought to be driving forces in a homologous human cancer. Genetic analyses demonstrated that EGFR and PI3K initiate malignant neoplastic transformation via a combinatorial genetic network composed primarily of other pathways commonly mutated or activated in human glioma, including the Tor, Myc, G1 Cyclins-Cdks, and Rb-E2F pathways. This network acts synergistically to coordinately stimulate cell cycle entry and progression, protein translation, and inappropriate cellular growth and migration. In particular, we found that the fly orthologs of CyclinE, Cdc25, and Myc are key rate-limiting genes required for glial neoplasia. Moreover, orthologs of Sin1, Rictor, and Cdk4 are genes required only for abnormal neoplastic glial proliferation but not for glial development. These and other genes within this network may represent important therapeutic targets in human glioma.
###end p 2
###begin title 3
Author Summary
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 530 553 530 553 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila melanogaster</italic>
###xml 632 642 632 642 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 828 838 828 838 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 103 108 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 519 528 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">fruit fly</span>
###xml 530 553 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila melanogaster</span>
###xml 770 775 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 967 972 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1185 1190 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1420 1425 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Malignant gliomas, tumors composed of glial cells and their precursors, are the most common and deadly human brain tumors. These tumors infiltrate the brain and proliferate rapidly, properties that render them largely incurable even with current therapies. Mutations in genes within the EGFR-Ras and PI3K signaling pathways are common in malignant gliomas, although how these genes specifically control glial pathogenesis is unclear. To investigate the genetic basis of this disease, we developed a glioma model in the fruit fly, Drosophila melanogaster. We found that constitutive coactivation of the EGFR-Ras and PI3K pathways in Drosophila glia gives rise to highly proliferative and invasive neoplastic cells that create transplantable tumor-like growths, mimicking human glioma. This represents a robust cell-type-specific Drosophila cancer model in which malignant cells are created by mutations in genetic pathways thought to be driving forces in a homologous human cancer. Genetic analyses demonstrated that EGFR-Ras and PI3K induce fly glial neoplasia through activation of a combinatorial genetic network composed, in part, of other genetic pathways also commonly mutated in human glioma. This network acts synergistically to coordinately stimulate cellular proliferation, protein translation, and inappropriate migration. Rate-limiting genes within this network may represent important therapeutic targets in human glioma.
###end p 4
###begin title 5
Introduction
###end title 5
###begin p 6
###xml 733 736 733 736 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Maher1">[1]</xref>
###xml 737 740 737 740 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Furnari1">[2]</xref>
###xml 983 986 979 982 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Maher1">[1]</xref>
###xml 987 990 983 986 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Furnari1">[2]</xref>
###xml 1060 1063 1056 1059 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Maher1">[1]</xref>
###xml 1064 1067 1060 1063 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Furnari1">[2]</xref>
###xml 1261 1264 1257 1260 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Furnari1">[2]</xref>
###xml 1265 1268 1261 1264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Holland1">[4]</xref>
Malignant gliomas, neoplasms of glial cells and their precursors, are the most common tumors of the central nervous system (CNS). These tumors typically proliferate rapidly, diffusely infiltrate the brain, and resist standard chemotherapies, properties that render them largely incurable. One key to developing more effective therapies against these tumors is to understand the genetic and molecular logic underlying gliomagenesis. The most frequent genetic lesions in gliomas include mutation or amplification of the Epidermal Growth Factor Receptor (EGFR) tyrosine kinase. Glioma-associated EGFR mutant forms show constitutive kinase activity that chronically stimulates Ras signaling to drive cellular proliferation and migration [1],[2]. Other common genetic lesions include loss of the lipid phosphatase PTEN, which antagonizes the phosphatidylinositol-3 kinase (PI3K) signaling pathway, and activating mutations in PIK3CA, which encodes the p110alpha catalytic subunit of PI3K [1],[2]. Gliomas often show constitutively active Akt, a major PI3K effector [1],[2]. However, EGFR-Ras or PI3K mutations alone are not sufficient to transform glial cells, rather multiple mutations that coactivate EGFR-Ras and PI3K-Akt pathways are sufficient to induce glioma [2]-[4].
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 529 532 529 532 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Maher1">[1]</xref>
###xml 788 791 788 791 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Singh1">[5]</xref>
###xml 792 795 792 795 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Bachoo1">[6]</xref>
###xml 625 630 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 774 779 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Understanding the interplay of these mutations and the neurodevelopmental origins of these tumors could lead to new insights into the mechanisms of gliomagenesis. The mammalian brain contains multiple glial cell types that maintain proliferative capacities, including differentiated astrocytes, glial progenitors, and multipotent neural stem cells. EGFR-Ras and PTEN-PI3K signaling regulates many developmental processes in these cell types, particularly proliferation and self-renewal, which are also properties of glioma cells [1]. Although recent hypotheses favor that gliomas arise from multipotent stem cells, data from mouse models demonstrate that differentiated glia, glial progenitors, and stem cells can all produce gliomas in response to genetic lesions found in human gliomas [5],[6]. Thus, misregulation of these genetic pathways may confer unrestricted proliferative capacities to a range of glial cell types, but how this occurs remains unclear. While many of the same effectors are utilized by EGFR-Ras and PI3K in both glial development and cancer, constitutive activation of these pathways may deploy distinct outputs, not utilized in development, that allow particular cells to escape normal physiological cues that restrain proliferation and self-renewal. The identity of such outputs remains unclear.
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 42 52 42 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 120 130 120 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 326 336 326 336 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 347 350 347 350 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Reiter1">[7]</xref>
###xml 481 491 481 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 671 674 671 674 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Bilen1">[8]</xref>
###xml 687 697 687 697 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 896 899 896 899 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Freeman1">[9]</xref>
###xml 950 960 950 960 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 259 264 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 526 531 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 938 944 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
With these issues in mind, we developed a Drosophila glioma model to facilitate genetic analysis of glial pathogenesis. Drosophila offers many tools for precise manipulation of cell-type-specific gene expression and dissection of multigene interactions. Most human genes, including 70% of known disease genes, have functional Drosophila orthologs [7]. Among the most conserved genes are components of major signal transduction pathways, including many gliomagenic genes. Recently, Drosophila has emerged as a model system for human neurological diseases because the CNS shows remarkable evolutionary conservation in cellular composition and neurodevelopmental mechanisms [8]. Similarly, Drosophila have multiple glial cell types that require the EGFR pathway for their normal development, and these cells appear homologous to mammalian glia in terms of function, development, and gene expression [9]. These similarities between flies and humans make Drosophila an attractive system for modeling gliomas.
###end p 8
###begin title 9
Results
###end title 9
###begin title 10
###xml 37 47 37 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
Coactivation of EGFR-Ras and PI3K in Drosophila Glia Causes Neoplasia
###end title 10
###begin p 11
###xml 107 110 107 110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Holland1">[4]</xref>
###xml 221 231 221 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 484 493 484 493 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 561 565 561 565 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Brand1">[10]</xref>
###xml 577 586 577 586 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4</italic>
###xml 758 762 758 762 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Dietzl1">[11]</xref>
###xml 834 855 834 855 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 927 931 927 931 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Lee1">[12]</xref>
###xml 1029 1038 1029 1038 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1053 1057 1053 1057 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Halter1">[13]</xref>
###xml 101 106 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Since concurrent activation of EGFR-Ras and PI3K signaling in glial precursors induces glioma in the mouse [4], we sought to create mutant phenotypes by hyperactivation of these pathways in fly glia and glial precursors. Drosophila has a single functional ortholog each for EGFR(dEGFR), Raf (dRaf), PIK3CA(dp110), PTEN(dPTEN), and Akt(dAkt), and two functional orthologs for Ras(dRas85D, dRas64B) (). A diagram of the specific mutant forms of dEGFR used in our assays can be found in Figure S1. We performed glial overexpression assays with the Gal4-UAS system [10], using the repo-Gal4 driver, which gives sustained UAS-transgene expression in almost all glia, from embryogenesis through adulthood. For glial-specific RNAi, we employed UAS-dsRNA constructs [11], which we verified with phenotypic tests and/or antibody staining (see Materials and Methods). Glial morphology was visualized with membrane-localized GFP (CD8GFP) [12]. Cell number was determined with staining for Repo, a homeobox transcription factor expressed by repo-Gal4 positive glia [13].
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 173 182 173 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4</italic>
###xml 233 239 233 234 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 257 261 252 256 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 333 349 316 332 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g001">Figure 1A and 1B</xref>
###xml 351 355 334 338 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Queenan1">[14]</xref>
###xml 356 360 339 343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Leevers1">[15]</xref>
###xml 367 373 350 351 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 487 491 465 469 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Queenan1">[14]</xref>
###xml 493 502 471 480 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 547 553 525 526 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 649 655 622 623 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 661 665 629 633 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 639 665 612 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 773 782 741 750 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 787 795 755 763 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s013">Table S1</xref>
###xml 899 902 867 870 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 930 933 898 901 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gof</sup>
###xml 945 949 913 917 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 967 972 935 940 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 1010 1019 978 987 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 1024 1032 992 1000 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s013">Table S1</xref>
###xml 1074 1080 1042 1043 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1086 1090 1049 1053 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 1064 1090 1032 1053 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 1208 1211 1171 1174 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N17</sup>
###xml 1214 1230 1177 1193 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g001">Figure 1D and 1E</xref>
Glial-specific coactivation of EGFR-Ras and PI3K stimulated glial neoplasia, giving rise to CNS enlargement and malformation, neurologic defects, and late larval lethality. repo-Gal4-driven co-overexpression of activated dEGFR (dEGFRlambda) and dp110 (dp110CAAX) induced progressive accumulation of approximately50-fold excess glia (Figure 1A and 1B) [14],[15]. dEGFRlambda is a constitutively active dEGFR variant in which a lambda dimerization domain replaces the extracellular domain [14] (Figure S1). Co-overexpression of combinations of dEGFRlambda and core components of the PI3K pathway, such as dAkt, induced phenotypes similar to repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX, although phenotypes varied somewhat depending on strength of pathway activation and transgene expression (Figure S2 and Table S1). Dramatic glial overgrowth also occurred upon co-overexpression of constitutively active dRas (dRas85DV12) or its effector dRaf (dRafgof) with dp110CAAX, dAkt, or a dPTENdsRNA, which partially knocked-down dPTEN (Figure S2 and Table S1). Finally, glial overgrowth in repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX larvae was strongly suppressed by co-overexpression of dPTEN or more moderately by dominant negative dRas85D (dRas85DN17) (Figure 1D and 1E), indicating that Ras activity and excess phospho-inositols are essential for neoplasia.
###end p 12
###begin title 13
###xml 37 47 37 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
Coactivation of EGFR-Ras and PI3K in Drosophila glia causes neoplasia.
###end title 13
###begin p 14
###xml 79 81 79 81 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rd</sup>
###xml 224 233 224 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4</italic>
###xml 342 348 342 343 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 354 358 349 353 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 332 358 332 353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 529 531 520 522 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rd</sup>
###xml 815 824 802 811 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4</italic>
###xml 839 845 826 827 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 851 855 833 837 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 829 855 816 837 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 967 970 949 952 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N17</sup>
###xml 976 982 958 959 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 988 992 965 969 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 958 992 940 969 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dRas<sup>N17</sup>;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 1017 1023 994 995 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1029 1033 1001 1005 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>

###xml 2250 2289 2187 2226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-dp110<sup>CAAX</sup>/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+</italic>
(A) Optical projections of whole brain-ventral nerve cord complexes from late 3rd instar larvae approximately 130 hr AED, displayed at the same scale. Dorsal view; anterior up. Glia are labeled with CD8GFP (green) driven by repo-Gal4. Each brain is composed of 2 symmetrical hemispheres attached to the ventral nerve cord (VNC). In repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX larvae, both brain hemispheres and the VNC are enlarged and elongated relative to other genotypes. (B-H) 2 microm optical sections of larval brain hemispheres from late 3rd instar larvae approximately 130 hr AED, displayed at the same scale. 20 microm scale bars. Frontal sections, midway through brains. Anterior up; midline to left. Glial cell nuclei are labeled with Repo (red). Glial cell bodies and membranes are labeled with CD8GFP (green) driven by repo-Gal4. In repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX brains (B) there is a dramatic increase in number of glial nuclei relative to wild-type (C), while in repo>dRasN17;dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX (D) and repo>PTEN; dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX (E) brains there are fewer excess glial nuclei. In wild-type animals (C), glia extend processes throughout the entire brain, enveloping nearly every cell with glial membranes. In contrast, dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia (B) show loss of fine projections and instead have compact cell bodies. Brains are counter-stained with anti-HRP (blue), which reveals neuronal fiber tracts (neuropil) at high intensity and some cell bodies of neurons and neuronal precursors at low intensity. HRP staining varies slightly according to exact plane of section, brain orientation, and mutant phenotype. Dark areas within brains contain unstained cells, which are typically optic lobe neural precursors. Genotypes: (A) Clockwise from top left: repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, UAS-dEGFRlambda/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (B) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (C) repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (D) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/UAS-dRas85DN17; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (E) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; UAS-PTEN/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (F) UAS-dEGFRlambda/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (G) repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-dRas85DV12, (H) UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+.
###end p 14

###xml 196 205 191 200 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g001">Figure 1F</xref>
###xml 210 218 205 213 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s013">Table S1</xref>
###xml 228 231 223 226 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>

###xml 367 376 357 366 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g001">Figure 1G</xref>
###xml 386 389 376 379 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>

###xml 513 516 498 501 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Elp</sup>
###xml 564 568 549 553 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Lesokhin1">[17]</xref>
###xml 639 648 624 633 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 719 722 704 707 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Elp</sup>
###xml 826 829 811 814 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Bachoo1">[6]</xref>
###xml 830 834 815 819 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Lesokhin1">[17]</xref>
###xml 869 878 854 863 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 893 899 878 879 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 906 908 886 888 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">WT</sup>
###xml 918 921 898 901 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Elp</sup>
###xml 962 971 942 951 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 1072 1076 1052 1056 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Lesokhin1">[17]</xref>
###xml 1164 1168 1144 1148 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 1175 1184 1155 1164 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">wild-type</sup>
###xml 1200 1205 1180 1185 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 1257 1266 1237 1246 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g001">Figure 1H</xref>
###xml 1268 1277 1248 1257 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 1283 1291 1263 1271 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s013">Table S1</xref>
###xml 749 754 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
In contrast, glial-specific activation of the EGFR-Ras pathway alone, through overexpression of dEGFRlambda or Rafgof, induced 5-10 fold excess glia in the larval brain and later pupal lethality (Figure 1F and Table S1). dRas85DV12 overexpression induced approximately 5-10-fold excess glia, and these glia were smaller than wild-type or dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia. (Figure 1G). dRas85DV12 may be more potent than dEGFRlambda because dRas85DV12 can activate endogenous PI3K signaling [16]. Overexpression of dEGFRElp, a classical hypermorphic mutant form of dEGFR [17], induced excess glial proliferation and neural morphogenesis defects (Figure S2), but also caused early lethality which precluded examination of dEGFRElp-dp110 interactions. As in mouse models, overexpression of wild-type dEGFR failed to induce excess glia [6],[17], and instead retarded CNS growth (Figure S2). Unlike dEGFRlambda, dEGFRWT and dEGFRElp have functional ligand-binding domains (Figure S1), and may cause additional defects by sequestering ligand otherwise required for normal development [17]. Glial-specific activation of the PI3K pathway alone, either by overexpression of dp110CAAX, dp110wild-type, dAkt, or dPTENdsRNA gave viable animals with relatively normal brains (Figure 1H, Figure S2, and Table S1). Therefore, coactivation of the EGFR and PI3K pathways synergize to produce much more severe phenotypes than would be expected if the effects of these pathways were additive.
###end p 15
###begin p 16
###xml 13 19 13 14 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 25 29 20 24 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 3 29 3 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 117 123 112 113 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 129 133 119 123 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 210 226 200 216 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g001">Figure 1A and 1B</xref>
###xml 231 242 221 232 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g002">Figure 2A&#8211;C</xref>
###xml 286 297 276 287 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g002">Figure 2A&#8211;C</xref>
###xml 378 389 368 379 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g002">Figure 2A&#8211;C</xref>
###xml 411 417 401 402 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 423 427 408 412 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 448 452 433 437 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Hariharan1">[18]</xref>
###xml 493 499 478 479 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 505 509 485 489 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 589 598 569 578 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s003">Figure S3</xref>
###xml 640 644 620 624 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Igaki1">[19]</xref>
###xml 645 649 625 629 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Uhlirova1">[20]</xref>
###xml 679 685 659 660 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 691 695 666 670 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 802 808 777 778 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 814 818 784 788 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 907 911 877 881 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Betschinger1">[21]</xref>
###xml 912 916 882 886 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Beaucher1">[22]</xref>
In repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX brains, excess glia emerged in early larval stages and accumulated over 5-7 days. dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia severely disrupt the normal cellular architecture of the larval brain (Figure 1A and 1B and Figure 2A-C), lose normal stellate glial morphologies (Figure 2A-C), and generate multilayered aggregations of abnormal glia throughout the brain (Figure 2A-C); in these ways dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia are neoplastic [18]. Like neoplastic epithelial cells, dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia ectopically expressed an active form of the matrix metalloprotease dMMP1 (Figure S3), which can confer an invasive potential [19],[20], implying that abnormal dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia may be invasive within the brain. Unlike neoplastic epithelia, neoplastic neural cells, such as dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia, typically retain expression of genes that regulate neural cell fate, such as Repo [21],[22].
###end p 16
###begin title 17
Coactivation of EGFR and PI3K cell-autonomously promotes cell cycle entry.
###end title 17
###begin p 18
###xml 25 27 25 27 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rd</sup>

###xml 660 664 651 655 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>

###xml 871 897 862 883 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 1341 1347 1327 1328 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>

###xml 1331 1357 1317 1338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 1865 1871 1842 1843 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1877 1881 1849 1853 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 2081 2087 2053 2054 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 2093 2097 2060 2064 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 2190 2196 2157 2158 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 2202 2206 2164 2168 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>

###xml 2422 2424 2372 2374 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rd</sup>

###xml 2743 2749 2688 2689 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>

###xml 2801 2812 2741 2752 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;CD8GFP</italic>
###xml 3022 3044 2962 2984 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+</italic>

###xml 3079 3134 3019 3069 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup> UAS-dp110<sup>CAAX</sup>/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+</italic>

###xml 3140 3201 3075 3131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup> UAS-dp110<sup>CAAX</sup>/UAS-dap; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+</italic>
###xml 3216 3222 3146 3147 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 3232 3236 3157 3161 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 3207 3269 3137 3194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;UAS-dp110<sup>CAAX</sup>/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-Rbf1</italic>
###xml 424 433 <span type="species:ncbi:119431">honeycomb</span>
(A-F) Close-ups of late 3rd instar larval brain hemispheres. Anterior up; midline to left. 20 microm scale bars. (A-C) Glial cell nuclei are labeled with Repo (red). Glial cell bodies and membranes are labeled with CD8GFP (green) driven by repo-Gal4. In wild-type (A), surface glia (SG) that cover the brain form a single-cell layer of fairly flat cells whereas astrocyte-like cortex glia are often evenly spaced and form a honeycomb-like network of fine projections throughout the brain. Superficial cortex glia show stellate morphology (arrowheads), and cortex glia deeper in the brain sometimes show a radial morphology (asterisk). In repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX brains (B,C) surface glia (SG) and superficial cortex glia (brighter GFP, arrowheads) form thick multicellular aggregations throughout the brain and often adopt a spindle-shaped morphology (arrowheads). In repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX brains, deeper cortex glia (C) can still form fine projections, but more often lack these and create loose aggregates of abnormally shaped cells (asterisks). (D,E) BrdU labeling (red) of S-phase cells. The prominent replicative cells in normal brains (D) are neuroblasts ('NB') and optic lobe neural precursors ('NP'), identified by their stereotyped position and/or staining for HRP (faint blue). The prominent replicative cells in repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX brains (E) are glia ('G'), which do not stain for HRP. 2 microm optical sections. (F-I) dCyclinE (F,G) and dCyclinB (H,I) expression (red) shown alone (left panels) and with Repo (blue nuclei) and CD8GFP (green, membranes/cytoplasm) glial markers (right in each panel). 'G' denotes representative glia, 'NB', representative neuroblasts. In wild-type (F, H), glia rarely expressed dCyclinE or dCyclinB, while neuroblasts ('NB') showed predominant expression. dCyclinE expression is primarily nuclear in dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia (G), visible as purple in overlay (right panel), although not all mutant glia express dCyclinE. Inset in (G) shows dCyclinE expression in polyploid glia ('ppG'). (I) dCyclinB expression in dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia is primarily cytoplasmic, visible as yellow in overlay (right panel). ppG in repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX brains do not express dCyclinB, as seen by the absence of yellow or purple in overlay. (F,G) 6.5 microm and (H,I) 5 microm optical projections. (J-M) 2 microm optical sections of larval brain hemispheres from late 3rd instar larvae approximately 130 hr AED, displayed at the same scale. Frontal sections, midway through brains. repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX brains (K) show a dramatic increase in number of glial nuclei (red) relative to wild-type (J). Glial cell nuclei are decreased by co-overexpression of Dap (L) or Rbf1 (M) with dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX. Glial cell bodies and membranes (green, repo>CD8GFP reporter) appear relatively normal in (L) and (M) compared to (J). HRP counter-stain (blue) reveals neuropil at high intensity and neuronal cell bodies at low intensity. Genotypes: (A), (D), (F), (H), and (J) repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (B), (C), (E), (G), (I), and (K) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (L) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/UAS-dap; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (M) UAS-dEGFRlambda;UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-Rbf1.
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 32 38 32 33 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 44 48 39 43 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 108 124 103 119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g002">Figure 2D and 2E</xref>
###xml 199 205 194 195 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 211 215 201 205 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 189 215 184 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 273 282 263 272 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g002">Figure 2E</xref>
###xml 541 545 531 535 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Lee2">[23]</xref>
###xml 993 997 983 987 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Lee2">[23]</xref>
Relative to controls, many dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia showed BrdU incorporation, which marks S-phase cells (Figure 2D and 2E), indicating that neoplastic glia arise from overproliferation. repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX animals also showed reduced BrdU in neuronal precursors (Figure 2E, data not shown), demonstrating that neoplastic glia disrupt neuronal development. The cell cycle is governed by CyclinD-Cdk4 and CyclinE-Cdk2 complexes, which phosphorylate and inactivate Rb proteins, to release E2F activators to stimulate G1-S-phase entry [23]. Kip-type (p21/p27/p57) and Ink-type cyclin-dependent kinase inhibitors antagonize proliferation by inhibiting CyclinE-Cdk2 and CyclinD-Cdk4, respectively. Cdc25 phosphatases and mitotic cyclins, including CyclinB, promote G2-M progression. Flies have single orthologs each for CyclinE, Cdk2, CyclinD, Cdk4, CyclinB, and p21/p27/p57 (Dap), E2F activators (E2F1) and two orthologs for Rb (Rbf1 and Rbf2) and Cdc25 (Stg and Twe) but no Ink ortholog [23].
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 5 11 5 6 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 17 21 12 16 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 79 90 74 85 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g002">Figure 2F&#8211;I</xref>
###xml 314 318 309 313 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Drummond1">[24]</xref>
###xml 341 347 336 337 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 353 357 343 347 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 331 357 326 347 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 486 492 476 477 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 498 502 483 487 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 476 502 466 487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 742 758 727 743 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g002">Figure 2G and 2I</xref>
###xml 989 998 974 983 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 214 219 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia showed ectopic expression of dCyclinE and dCyclinB (Figure 2F-I), demonstrating that EGFR and PI3K activity upregulated proteins that promote cell cycle entry and progression. High-grade human gliomas contain highly proliferative anaplastic glia and enlarged pleiomorphic polyploid glia [24]. Similarly, repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX larvae showed accumulation of small, highly proliferative glia that strongly expressed cyclins and labeled with BrdU. repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX larval brains also displayed abnormal polyploid glia, as assessed by DAPI staining (data not shown), and these cells typically expressed only dCyclinE but not dCyclinB, and thereby likely underwent ectopic DNA replication without mitosis (Figure 2G and 2I, data not shown). However, overexpression of dCyclinE-dCdk2, dCyclinD-dCdk4, or dE2F1-dDp complexes and/or Rbf1 knock-down did not cause neoplasia, and instead either doubled glial cell numbers or resulted in embryonic lethality (Figure S4, data not shown).
###end p 20
###begin p 21
###xml 61 67 61 62 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 73 77 68 72 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 167 176 162 171 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s005">Figure S5</xref>
###xml 216 220 211 215 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-deNooij1">[25]</xref>
###xml 330 334 325 329 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Wallace1">[26]</xref>
###xml 387 393 382 383 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 399 403 389 393 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 377 403 372 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 422 431 412 421 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g002">Figure 2L</xref>
###xml 542 546 532 536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rbf1</italic>
###xml 551 559 541 549 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dCyclinE</italic>
###xml 593 599 583 584 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 605 609 590 594 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 583 609 573 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 635 644 620 629 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g002">Figure 2M</xref>
###xml 724 730 709 710 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 736 740 716 720 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 714 740 699 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 869 880 849 860 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g002">Figure 2J&#8211;M</xref>
###xml 896 902 876 877 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 908 912 883 887 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 886 912 866 887 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 1204 1213 1179 1188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 1301 1310 1276 1285 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1395 1399 1370 1374 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Chotard1">[27]</xref>
###xml 1400 1404 1375 1379 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Stork1">[28]</xref>
We next examined negative regulators of the cell cycle. dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia expressed Rbf1, but showed little Dap, a result we also observed in wild-type glia (Figure S5). Dap inhibits dCyclinE-cdk2 complexes [25], and is transiently expressed in neural progenitors to promote cell cycle exit as they begin differentiation [26]. Dap overexpression completely suppressed repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glial overgrowth (Figure 2L), demonstrating that glial neoplasia is cell-autonomous and requires dCyclinE-dCdk2. Similarly, overexpressed Rbf1 and dCyclinE mutations also reduced repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glial overproliferation (Figure 2M, data not shown). The gross neural morphogenesis defects observed in repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX brains may be secondary to glial overproliferation since these defects were largely prevented by Dap or Rbf1 co-overexpression (Figure 2J-M). In repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX animals, other mutant glia outside of the brain, such as peripheral glia, also became highly proliferative and invasive, and these defects, too, were corrected by Rbf1 or Dap overexpression (data not shown). In controls, Rbf1 or Dap overexpression in wild-type glia inhibited proliferation (Figure S4), reducing numbers of glia by approximately half. Together, these results suggest that repo-Gal4 glia undergo at least one round of cell division, consistent with published studies [27],[28], and this proliferation becomes prolonged by constitutive coactivation of EGFR and PI3K signaling.
###end p 21
###begin title 22
Coactivation of EGFR and PI3K Does Not Elicit Neoplasia in All Neural Cell Types
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 88 98 88 98 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>

###xml 197 201 197 201 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Caussinus1">[29]</xref>

###xml 716 724 706 714 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s014">Table S2</xref>
###xml 747 750 737 740 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 845 849 835 839 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Voas1">[30]</xref>
###xml 850 854 840 844 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Karim1">[31]</xref>
###xml 882 888 872 873 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 899 902 884 887 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 913 917 898 902 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 930 939 915 924 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">elav-Gal4</italic>
###xml 941 953 926 938 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">scratch-Gal4</italic>
###xml 955 965 940 950 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">OK107-Gal4</italic>
###xml 971 980 956 965 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Appl-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1019 1028 1004 1013 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pros-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1030 1038 1015 1023 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">wor-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1044 1053 1029 1038 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1407-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1082 1091 1067 1076 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s007">Figure S7</xref>
###xml 1175 1179 1160 1164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Hassan1">[32]</xref>
###xml 1222 1228 1207 1208 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1238 1242 1218 1222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 1283 1292 1263 1272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pros-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1450 1454 1430 1434 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Halfar1">[33]</xref>
###xml 1500 1503 1480 1483 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 1512 1518 1492 1493 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1528 1532 1503 1507 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 1552 1560 1527 1535 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gcm-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1603 1612 1578 1587 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s007">Figure S7</xref>
###xml 1614 1618 1589 1593 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Chotard1">[27]</xref>
###xml 1787 1797 1762 1772 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eaat1-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1833 1842 1808 1817 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nrv2-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1878 1886 1853 1861 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gli-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1955 1964 1930 1939 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s007">Figure S7</xref>
###xml 1982 1986 1957 1961 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Sun1">[34]</xref>
###xml 1987 1991 1962 1966 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Lavery1">[36]</xref>
The phenotype triggered by coactivation of EGFR and PI3K in glia is distinct from other Drosophila brain-overgrowth mutant phenotypes, which involve accretion of excess neurons or neuroblasts [21],[29]. repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX cells were not transformed into neurons or neuroblasts as they lacked expression of the Elav and Miranda markers (Figure S6). Lineage-tracing with a Su(H)-lacZ neuroblast reporter showed that excess dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia did not express LacZ, and thus are not directly derived from larval neuroblasts (data not shown). Moreover, constitutive EGFR-Ras and PI3K signaling does not elicit overgrowth in all neural cell types, as assessed with defined cell-type specific Gal4-drivers (Table S2). For example, dRas85DV12 overexpression in fly neurons causes defects in fate specification, patterning, and apoptosis [30],[31]. Co-overexpression of dEGFRlambda or dRas85DV12 with dp110CAAX in neurons (elav-Gal4, scratch-Gal4, OK107-Gal4, and Appl-Gal4) and neuroblasts/neuronal precursors (pros-Gal4, wor-Gal4, and 1407-Gal4) did not induce overgrowth (Figure S7, data not shown), even with increased transgene expression from Gal4 amplification [32]. In fact, broad co-overexpression of dEGFRlambda and dp110CAAX in neuroblasts and neuronal precursors (pros-Gal4) reduced brain size, perhaps because signaling through these pathways stimulates precocious cell cycle exit of neuronal precursors, as in the developing eye [33]. Furthermore, transient expression of dRas85DV12 or dEGFRlambda and dp110CAAX in embryonic glia (gcm-Gal4) also failed to promote glial overgrowth (Figure S7) [27], demonstrating that sustained activation of these pathways is required for glial overproliferation. Certain glial subtypes, such as oligodendrocyte-like neuropil glia (Eaat1-Gal4), some astrocyte-like cortex glia (Nrv2-Gal4), and peripheral perineurial glia (gli-Gal4) also failed to become neoplastic in response to EGFR-Ras and PI3K (Figure S7, data not shown) [34]-[36]. Therefore, neoplastic proliferation is not a uniform cellular response to EGFR and PI3K.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
Coactivation of EGFR and PI3K Inhibits Cell Cycle Exit in Glia
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 16 22 16 17 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 28 32 23 27 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 6 32 6 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 191 195 186 190 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Woodhouse1">[37]</xref>
###xml 228 234 223 224 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 240 244 230 234 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 218 244 213 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 382 398 372 388 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g003">Figure 3A and 3C</xref>
###xml 406 412 396 397 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 418 422 403 407 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 545 554 530 539 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g003">Figure 3B</xref>
###xml 622 633 607 618 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g003">Figure 3D&#8211;F</xref>
###xml 698 714 683 699 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g003">Figure 3D and 3E</xref>
###xml 719 727 704 712 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s016">Video S1</xref>
###xml 968 977 953 962 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g003">Figure 3F</xref>
###xml 982 990 967 975 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s017">Video S2</xref>
###xml 1074 1080 1059 1060 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1086 1090 1066 1070 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 1117 1126 1097 1106 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s003">Figure S3</xref>
###xml 1297 1303 1277 1278 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1309 1313 1284 1288 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 1424 1429 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Since repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX animals die in 5-7 days, we assessed the proliferative potential of mutant glia using an abdominal transplant assay, a classic test of tumorigencity in flies [37]. Brain fragments from repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX and wild-type larvae were transplanted into young adults. Wild-type transplants grew and survived over 1-6 weeks, but produced few glia (Figure 3A and 3C). dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX mutant glia survived and proliferated into massive tumors that filled the hosts' abdomens, often causing premature death (Figure 3B). Tumors were composed of small glial cells with little cytoplasm (Figure 3D-F). Tumors also contained trachea embedded throughout their mass (Figure 3D and 3E and Video S1), suggesting that tumors stimulated growth of new trachea or enveloped existing trachea, perhaps in a process akin to tumor angiogenesis. The leading edges of the tumors harbored individual cells invading nearby tissues, such as the ovary (Figure 3F and Video S2), which is consistent with the ectopic expression of active dMMP1 observed in dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia in the larval brain (Figure S3). However, some tissues, such as the gut, did not contain metastases, implying some degree of selective invasion. Thus, once unconstrained by the larval life cycle, dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia fail to exit the cell cycle, continue to proliferate, and form highly invasive tumors, all properties of human cancer cells.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
Coactivation of EGFR and PI3K inhibits cell cycle exit in glia.
###end title 26
###begin p 27
###xml 327 333 327 328 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 339 343 334 338 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 494 500 481 482 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 506 510 488 492 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 660 666 642 643 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 672 676 649 653 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 800 806 777 778 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 812 816 784 788 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 986 990 950 954 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1118</sup>
###xml 985 990 949 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">w<sup>1118</sup></italic>
###xml 1049 1074 1013 1038 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-CD8GFP/+; repo-Gal4/+</italic>
###xml 1108 1114 1072 1073 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1124 1128 1083 1087 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 1099 1157 1063 1116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup> UAS-dp110<sup>CAAX</sup>/+; UAS-CD8GFP/+; repo-Gal4/+</italic>
Larval brain fragments of the indicated genotypes were injected into the abdomens of wild-type adult hosts and grown for 3 weeks. CD8GFP (green) labels all transplanted glia within each graft. Actin (red, phalloidin) reveals abdominal anatomy. (A, B) Representative frozen sections of whole abdomens with wild-type (A) or dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX (B) transplants, shown at the same scale. 50 microm optical projections; 100 microm scale bars. (C-F) Transplants shown at higher magnification. dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX transplants (D-F) are rich with glial cell nuclei (Repo, in blue) relative to wild-type transplants (C). Asterisks indicate trachea embedded in dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX transplants (D,E), visible as hollow actin-positive (red) tubules running through tissues. Arrowheads in (F) indicate dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glial cells invading an ovary, distinguished by its characteristic actin staining (red). 1-1.5 microm optical sections; 20 microm scale bars. Genotypes: All hosts were w1118 virgin females. Transplanted glia as follows: (A) and (C) UAS-CD8GFP/+; repo-Gal4/+, (B), (D), (E), and (F) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; UAS-CD8GFP/+; repo-Gal4/+.
###end p 27
###begin title 28
Coactivation of EGFR-Ras and PI3K Creates Invasive Neoplastic Glia
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 459 468 459 468 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4</italic>
###xml 486 490 486 490 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Lee1">[12]</xref>
To explore the invasive potential of mutant glia, we used FLP-FRT clonal analysis, a technique in which discrete clones of mutant cells are induced in otherwise normal tissues, a situation analogous to somatic tumorigenesis. We used a heat-shock-driven FLP-recombinase to catalyze mitotic recombination between FRT-bearing chromosomes such that a daughter cell (and all of its clonal progeny) initiated expression of GFP and UAS-containing transgenes only in repo-Gal4-expressing cells [12]. Clones were induced late in development, from mitotic founder cells, and were examined in adults. We could not definitively determine if clones were derived from single cell events since our study of these clones was retrospective, but given the frequency of control clone induction, many mutant clones likely originated from single cells.
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 200 216 200 216 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4A and 4B</xref>
###xml 254 257 254 257 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 264 270 264 265 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 280 283 275 278 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Elp</sup>
###xml 351 354 346 349 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 364 373 359 368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4C</xref>
###xml 413 418 408 413 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dPTEN</italic>
###xml 480 483 475 478 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 475 483 470 478 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 554 563 549 558 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4D</xref>
###xml 620 624 615 619 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-vonStein1">[38]</xref>
In wild-type controls, we observed clones in 68% of brains examined (N = 149). Of the brains with clones, 75% had 1-3 clones, and 83% of these clones consisted of 1-3 cells of the same glial subtype (Figure 4A and 4B). Glial clones overexpressing dRas85DV12, dEGFRlambda, or dEGFRElp alone typically contained 2-fold more cells than wild-type (dRas85DV12 shown in Figure 4C). To examine PI3K signaling, we used a dPTEN null allele, which became homozygous in FLP-FRT clones. dPTEN-/- glia did not overgrow, but did show aberrant cytoplasmic projections (Figure 4D), perhaps reflecting dPTEN function in the cytoskeleton [38].
###end p 30
###begin title 31
Coactivation of EGFR-Ras and PI3K creates invasive neoplastic glia.
###end title 31
###begin p 32
###xml 18 27 18 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4</italic>
###xml 643 646 639 642 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 636 647 632 643 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRas85D<sup>V12</sup>-</italic>
###xml 706 709 702 705 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 699 709 695 705 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRas85D<sup>V12</sup></italic>
###xml 853 856 849 852 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 848 856 844 852 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 937 940 933 936 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>

###xml 930 949 926 945 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRas85D<sup>V12</sup>; PTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1124 1132 1120 1128 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s018">Video S3</xref>
###xml 1199 1205 1195 1196 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>

###xml 1224 1227 1215 1218 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Elp</sup>
###xml 1233 1236 1224 1227 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1219 1236 1210 1227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dEGFR<sup>Elp</sup>;dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1300 1303 1291 1294 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 1309 1312 1300 1303 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1293 1312 1284 1303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRas85D<sup>V12</sup>; PTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1403 1409 1390 1396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ey-FLP</italic>
###xml 1414 1423 1401 1410 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1569 1572 1552 1555 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 1562 1572 1545 1555 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRas85D<sup>V12</sup></italic>
###xml 1586 1589 1569 1572 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1581 1589 1564 1572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
