###xml 2812 2815 2790 2793 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">40A</sup>
###xml 2820 2825 2798 2803 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2L117</sup>
###xml 2859 2862 2837 2840 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 2783 2862 2761 2840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ey-flp/+; FRT<sup>40A</sup> tubGal80/FRT<sup>40A</sup> PTEN<sup>2L117</sup>; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-dRas85D<sup>V12</sup></italic>
FLP/FRT clones of repo-Gal4-expressing glia within whole adult brains, all displayed at the same scale. CD8GFP (green) labels the cell bodies and membranes of glial clones derived by FLP/FRT mitotic recombination (see text). Repo (red) labels all glial cell nuclei, in both clones and surrounding normal tissue. Red flare is background flourescence in (C-F). Frontal sections; anterior up; midline to left. 20 microm scale bars. (A-G) hs-FLP clones from approximately 2 week-old adults, heat-shocked as late pupae or young adults. (A-B) GFP-positive wild-type control clones composed of 1-3 cells with normal stellate morphology. (C) a dRas85DV12-expressing clone in the same brain region as (D,E). dRas85DV12 clones typically display the most proliferation among single mutant clones, containing approximately 2-5x more cells than controls. (D) a dPTEN-/- clone with abnormal morphology and punctate membrane-bound CD8GFP. (E) a dRas85DV12; PTEN-/- double mutant clone, composed of hundreds of cells that have overtaken the optic lobe and invaded the central brain (arrow), extending through the entire depth of the brain (Video S3). Asterisks demark optically opaque tracheal branches. (F,G) dEGFRlambda;dPTEN-/- and dEGFRElp;dPTEN-/- clones, which typically have less cellular density than dRas85DV12; PTEN-/- clones. 5-10 microm optical projections. (H-L) ey-FLP clones derived from a population of ey-FLP and repo-Gal4-expressing mitotic cells. (H-J,L) 8.5 microm confocal optical projections of whole optic lobes from brains of similarly aged adults. Both dRas85DV12 (I) and dPTEN-/- (J) clones contain 2-5-fold more cells than wild-type controls (H). dRas85DV12; PTEN-/- double mutant clones (L) form large glial tumors. White-bordered cut-out shows the high density of glial cell nuclei (red) in dRas85DV12; PTEN-/- double mutant clones (L). (K) shows an earlier stage dRas85DV12; PTEN-/- clone in the larval brain, where dRas85DV12; PTEN-/- clones begin as clusters of tens of cells, and grow to become large clones of hundreds of cells by early adulthood, as in (L). Genotypes: (A) and (B) hs-flp1/+;FRTG13 tubGal80/FRTG13 UAS-CD8GFP; repo-Gal4/+, (C) hs-flp1/+; FRTG13 tubGal80/FRTG13 UAS-CD8GFP; repo-Gal4/UAS-dRas85DV12, (D) hs-flp1/+; FRT40A tubGal80/FRT40A PTEN2L117; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (E) hs-flp1/+; FRT40A tubGal80/FRT40A PTEN2L117; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-dRas85DV12, (F) hs-flp1/+; FRT40A tubGal80/FRT40A PTEN2L117; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-dEGFRlambda, (G) hs-flp1/+; FRT40A tubGal80/FRT40A PTEN2L117; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-dEGFRElp, (H) ey-flp/+; FRT40A tubGal80/FRT40A; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (I) ey-flp/+; FRTG13 tubGal80/FRTG13 UAS-CD8GFP; repo-Gal4/UAS-dRas85DV12, (J) ey-flp/+; FRT40A tubGal80/FRT40A PTEN2L117; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (K and L) ey-flp/+; FRT40A tubGal80/FRT40A PTEN2L117; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-dRas85DV12.
###end p 32
###begin p 33
###xml 56 59 56 59 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 66 69 66 69 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Elp</sup>
###xml 79 85 79 80 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 116 119 111 114 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 111 119 106 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 132 141 127 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4</italic>
###xml 185 188 180 183 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 194 197 189 192 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 178 197 173 192 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRas85D<sup>V12</sup>;dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 207 210 202 205 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Elp</sup>
###xml 216 219 211 214 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 202 219 197 214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dEGFR<sup>Elp</sup>;dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 228 239 223 234 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4E&#8211;G</xref>
###xml 253 256 248 251 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 242 256 237 251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dEGFR;dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 284 300 279 295 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4F and 4G</xref>
###xml 355 358 350 353 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 459 462 454 457 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 440 462 435 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dEGFR-dRas85D;dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 726 735 721 730 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4E</xref>
###xml 779 782 774 777 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 760 782 755 777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dEGFR-dRas85D;dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 845 854 840 849 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s018">Videos S3</xref>
###xml 859 861 854 856 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s019">S4</xref>
###xml 932 935 923 926 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 925 935 916 926 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRas85D<sup>V12</sup></italic>
###xml 941 944 932 935 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 936 944 927 935 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 954 963 945 954 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4E</xref>
###xml 1034 1043 1021 1030 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
###xml 1125 1129 1112 1116 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Drummond1">[24]</xref>
###xml 1184 1187 1171 1174 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1165 1187 1152 1174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dEGFR-dRas85D;dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1285 1294 1272 1281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4G</xref>
###xml 1111 1116 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
To coactivate EGFR-Ras and PI3K in glial clones, dRas85DV12, dEGFRElp, or dEGFRlambda was overexpressed within dPTEN-/- glia, using repo-Gal4. We observed overgrown and invasive dRas85DV12;dPTEN-/- and dEGFRElp;dPTEN-/- clones (Figure 4E-G). dEGFR;dPTEN-/- clones were less affected (Figure 4F and 4G), consistent with the larval overexpression of dRas85DV12 giving more severe growth phenotypes. Tumor-like overgrowth was only observed in dEGFR-dRas85D;dPTEN-/- cells, illustrating that chronic EGFR-Ras activation and PTEN loss can cause cell-autonomous over-proliferation. Cells from these double mutant clones appeared to invade the brain, typically following fiber tracts, and sometimes induced the formation of trachea (Figure 4E). Tumor-like growths of dEGFR-dRas85D;dPTEN-/- cells often penetrated deep into the brain, as exemplified by Videos S3 and S4 which show an animated 88 microm thick confocal z-stack of the dRas85DV12;dPTEN-/- clone in Figure 4E compared to a 16 microm thick z-stack of a wild-type control clone in Figure 4A. These phenotypes were reminiscent of invasion and angiogenesis in human gliomas [24]. We more commonly observed smaller dEGFR-dRas85D;dPTEN-/- clones composed of relatively differentiated, enlarged glia with diffusely invasive projections (Figure 4G); these clones likely derive from glia that differentiated prior to achieving sufficient EGFR-Ras transgene expression, and are consistent with findings that not all glial subtypes become neoplastic.
###end p 33
###begin p 34
###xml 183 187 183 187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Chotard1">[27]</xref>
###xml 188 192 188 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Stork1">[28]</xref>
###xml 193 197 193 197 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Colonques1">[39]</xref>
###xml 402 406 402 406 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Chotard1">[27]</xref>
###xml 444 447 444 447 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 439 448 439 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>,</italic>
###xml 456 459 456 459 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 469 472 469 472 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Elp</sup>
###xml 565 576 565 576 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4H&#8211;J</xref>
###xml 581 590 581 590 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s008">Figure S8</xref>
###xml 631 634 631 634 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V12</sup>
###xml 640 643 640 643 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 624 643 624 643 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRas85D<sup>V12</sup>;dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 650 653 650 653 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Elp</sup>
###xml 659 662 659 662 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 645 662 645 662 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dEGFR<sup>Elp</sup>;dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 672 678 672 673 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 684 687 679 682 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 667 687 667 682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dPTEN<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 751 753 746 748 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rd</sup>
###xml 776 785 771 780 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4K</xref>
###xml 871 880 866 875 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g004">Figure 4L</xref>
###xml 885 894 880 889 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s008">Figure S8</xref>
Since neoplastic larval glia were concentrated in the outer anterior central brain and developing optic lobe, they may be derived from glial progenitor cells present in these regions [27],[28],[39]. To create clones from a discrete subpopulation of glial progenitors, we used an eyeless(ey)-promoter driven FLP-recombinase (ey-FLP), which is active in ey-expressing glial progenitors in the optic lobe [27]. Single mutant ey-FLP clones of dPTEN-/-, dRas85DV12, or dEGFRElp cells contained a modest number of excess and abnormal glia relative to wild-type controls (Figure 4H-J and Figure S8). In contrast, the double mutant dRas85DV12;dPTEN-/-, dEGFRElp;dPTEN-/-, or dEGFRlambda;dPTEN-/- ey-FLP clones, which emerge as approximately tens of cells in 3rd instar larval brains (Figure 4K), became large invasive tumors composed of hundreds to thousands of cells in adults (Figure 4L and Figure S8).
###end p 34
###begin title 35
EGFR;PI3K Induces Glial Neoplasia via Pnt and Stg Expression
###end title 35
###begin p 36
###xml 125 131 125 126 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 137 141 132 136 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 115 141 115 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 243 248 238 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dEGFR</italic>
###xml 253 258 248 253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dPTEN</italic>
###xml 201 206 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
To address the function of EGFR-Ras and PI3K in glioma, we analyzed the genetic basis of glial pathogenesis in our repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX model, as this model shows robust neoplasia, similarity to human tumor genotypes, and sensitivity to dEGFR and dPTEN gene dosage (data not shown).
###end p 36
###begin p 37
###xml 116 122 116 117 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 128 132 123 127 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 106 132 106 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 255 271 250 266 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g005">Figure 5A and 5B</xref>
###xml 379 386 374 381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pointed</italic>
###xml 388 391 383 386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pnt</italic>
###xml 399 403 394 398 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Klaes1">[40]</xref>
###xml 404 408 399 403 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Baonza1">[41]</xref>
###xml 499 503 494 498 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Klaes1">[40]</xref>
###xml 529 535 524 525 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 541 545 531 535 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 552 568 542 558 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g005">Figure 5C and 5D</xref>
###xml 895 899 885 889 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Baonza1">[41]</xref>
###xml 935 938 925 928 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pnt</italic>
###xml 993 999 983 984 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1005 1009 990 994 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 1021 1032 1006 1017 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g005">Figure 5E&#8211;H</xref>
###xml 1145 1151 1130 1131 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1157 1161 1137 1141 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 1188 1193 1168 1173 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 1199 1205 1179 1180 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1211 1215 1186 1190 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 1180 1215 1160 1190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;pnt<sup>dsRNA</sup>;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 1268 1277 1243 1252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo-Gal4</italic>
EGFR-Ras signaling can promote proliferation through Erk kinase-mediated induction of nuclear targets. In repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX brains, mutant glia showed high levels of nuclear, activated di-phospho-Erk relative to wild-type glia in control brains (Figure 5A and 5B). In flies, Erk activity can induce expression of PntP1, an ETS-family transcription factor encoded by the pointed (pnt) locus [40],[41]. PntP1, which is expressed in embryonic glia and is required for their normal development [40], was upregulated in dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia (Figure 5C and 5D). High levels of PntP1 can be detected normally in neuronal progenitors (data not shown), suggesting that it promotes a proliferative progenitor state. In developing eye tissue, EGFR-Ras-Erk signaling induces Pnt proteins to stimulate G2-M cell cycle progression through direct upregulation of Stg (Cdc25 ortholog) expression [41]. Glial-specific RNAi knock down of pnt reduced Stg expression and completely suppressed dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX neoplasia (Figure 5E-H), demonstrating that Pnt proteins are required for both Stg expression and neoplastic overproliferation in dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia. Notably, in repo>pntdsRNA;dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX brains, glia maintained their fate, as evidenced by repo-Gal4 and Repo expression.
###end p 37

###xml 2468 2473 2373 2378 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 2417 2494 2327 2399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup> UAS-dp110<sup>CAAX</sup>/+; stg<sup>CB03726</sup> UAS-pnt<sup>dsRNA</sup>/repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP</italic>
(A-D,F-H) late 3rd instar larval brain hemispheres. Staining patterns are shown alone (left panels) and with overlaid repo-Gal4-driven CD8GFP (green) and/or Repo (blue) glial markers (right panels). Close-ups of medial anterior regions; anterior up; midline to left. 20 microm scale bars. (A,B): Diphospho-ERK (P-ERK, red) staining in wild-type (A) and repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX (B) brains. High levels of nuclear ERK (arrows) are present in dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia, but not in wild-type glia. Glial cell bodies are labeled green in overlay (right panels). 2 microm optical sections. (C,D): PntP1 expression (red) in wild-type (C) and repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX (D) brains. Intense PntP1 expression in dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glial nuclei (arrows) is coincident with Repo and visible as purple nuclei in overlay (D, right panel). 3 microm optical projections. (E) Optical projections of whole brain-ventral nerve cord complexes from late 3rd instar larvae of the indicated genotype, approximately 130 hr AED, all matched in scale. CD8GFP (green) expression in all repo-Gal4-expressing glia reveals structure of the entire CNS. 200 microm scale bar. (F-H): Stg expression (red) in wild-type (F), repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX (G), and repo>pntdsRNA;dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX (H) brains. Stg expression in glia is visible as purple nuclei in overlay (right panels). repo>pntdsRNA;dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia (H) show reduced Stg compared to repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia (G, arrows indicate some Stg-expressing glia). Intense Stg expression (red only) in neuroblasts ('NB') and ganglion mother cell neuronal progenitors ('NP') is visible in all panels. Stg is visualized with the stgCB03726 protein trap, a viable stg allele that contains a GFP-expressing exon [68] and reflects the observed patterns of endogenous stg expression (data not shown). 5 microm optical projections. Genotypes: (A), (C), and (F) repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (B), (D), and (G) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (E) from left to right: repo-Gal4, UAS-CD8GFP/+, UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-pntdsRNA, UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/stg01235, UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; UAS-stg/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (F) stgCB03726/repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP, (G) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; stgCB03726/repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP, (H) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; stgCB03726 UAS-pntdsRNA/repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP.
###end p 39
###begin p 40
###xml 63 66 63 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">stg</italic>
###xml 91 96 91 96 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 88 96 88 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">stg<sup>dsRNA</sup></italic>
###xml 132 138 132 133 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 144 148 139 143 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 122 148 122 143 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 222 231 217 226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g005">Figure 5E</xref>
###xml 236 245 231 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s009">Figure S9</xref>
###xml 447 453 442 443 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 459 463 449 453 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 621 625 611 615 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Baonza1">[41]</xref>
###xml 626 630 616 620 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Prober2">[42]</xref>
Stg itself was rate limiting for glial neoplasia. Reduction of stg with a mutation or a stgdsRNA partially suppressed the repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX phenotype, whereas overexpressed Stg synergistically enhanced neoplasia (Figure 5E and Figure S9, data not shown). In contrast, Stg overexpression alone increased glial cell numbers approximately 2-fold, and could not induce neoplasia when combined with PI3K effectors (data not shown). Thus, dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX induces neoplasia via coordinated stimulation of G1-S entry through dCyclinE, and G2-M progression through Stg, both of which are EGFR-Ras dependent outputs [41],[42].
###end p 40
###begin title 41
EGFR;PI3K Glial Neoplasia Requires Akt and Tor Activation and FoxO Inactivation
###end title 41
###begin p 42
###xml 72 78 72 73 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 84 88 79 83 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 62 88 62 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 172 177 167 172 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 168 177 163 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dAkt<sup>dsRNA</sup></italic>
###xml 227 233 222 223 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 239 243 229 233 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 217 243 212 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 261 272 251 262 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g006">Figure 6A&#8211;C</xref>
###xml 459 467 449 457 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s015">Table S3</xref>
We sought to determine which PI3K effectors contribute to the repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX phenotype. Genetic reduction of dAkt, a major target of PI3K signaling, with a dAktdsRNA or a mutant allele strongly suppressed repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glial neoplasia (Figure 6A-C, data not shown). Therefore, Akt is necessary for the outcome of EGFR-PI3K coactivation. Many Akt effectors are implicated in glioma, and we tested orthologs of these loci in our model (Table S3).
###end p 42

###xml 1898 1904 1800 1801 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>

###xml 1979 1985 1876 1877 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>

###xml 2107 2112 1994 1999 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 2043 2112 1935 1999 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup> UAS-dp110<sup>CAAX</sup>/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-deIF4E<sup>dsRNA</sup></italic>
###xml 2127 2133 2014 2015 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 2143 2147 2025 2029 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 2118 2186 2005 2068 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup> UAS-dp110<sup>CAAX</sup>/+; UAS-d4EBP/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+</italic>

###begin p 45
###xml 218 222 218 222 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Hu1">[43]</xref>
###xml 223 227 223 227 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Pelloski1">[44]</xref>
###xml 250 260 250 260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 332 338 332 333 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 344 348 339 343 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 322 348 322 343 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 397 401 392 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dTor</italic>
###xml 460 462 455 457 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Luong1">45</xref>
###xml 463 465 458 460 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Hennig1">46</xref>
###xml 521 530 516 525 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g006">Figure 6D</xref>
###xml 155 161 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 200 207 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patient</span>
Tor, a kinase that promotes cell growth and proliferation, is a key Akt target. In glioma models, coactivation of EGFR-Ras and PI3K stimulates Tor, and in humans, Tor activity is correlated with poor patient prognosis [43],[44]. We tested the single Drosophila Tor ortholog, dTor, by genetically reducing dTor activity in repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX larvae with a viable combination of hypomorphic dTor alleles or by co-overexpression of dominant negative dTor 45,46. Both of these manipulations reduced glial overgrowth (Figure 6D, data not shown).
###end p 45
###begin p 46
###xml 252 256 252 256 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Guertin1">[47]</xref>
###xml 268 272 268 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sin1</italic>
###xml 277 283 277 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rictor</italic>
###xml 337 342 337 342 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dSin1</italic>
###xml 347 354 347 354 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRictor</italic>
###xml 449 453 449 453 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Guertin1">[47]</xref>
###xml 454 458 454 458 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Hietakangas1">[48]</xref>
###xml 465 468 465 468 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 480 486 480 481 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 492 496 487 491 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 460 496 460 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dSin1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>; repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 546 555 541 550 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g006">Figure 6E</xref>
###xml 586 593 581 588 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRictor</italic>
###xml 617 622 612 617 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 612 622 607 617 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dSin1<sup>dsRNA</sup></italic>
###xml 646 649 641 644 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 641 649 636 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dSin1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 661 664 656 659 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 654 664 649 659 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRictor<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 745 749 740 744 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Teleman1">[49]</xref>
###xml 762 772 757 767 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 925 927 920 922 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SA</sup>
###xml 972 976 967 971 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Luong1">[45]</xref>
###xml 1014 1020 1009 1010 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1026 1030 1016 1020 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 1004 1030 999 1020 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 1056 1065 1046 1055 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g006">Figure 6F</xref>
###xml 1137 1140 1127 1130 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1132 1140 1122 1130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dSin1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1152 1155 1142 1145 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1145 1155 1135 1145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dRictor<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1212 1221 1202 1211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g006">Figure 6G</xref>
###xml 1323 1329 1313 1314 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 1335 1339 1320 1324 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 261 266 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
In flies and mammals, Tor exists in two different signaling complexes, TORC1 and TORC2. TORC2, a complex including Tor and the Sin1 and Rictor regulatory proteins, directly phosphorylates Akt, creating a positive feedback loop that fully activates Akt [47]. In mouse, Sin1 and Rictor mutants die early due to extraembryonic defects, but dSin1 and dRictor mutant flies are viable as homozygous nulls, allowing us to remove TORC2 function genetically [47],[48]. dSin1-/-; repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX larval brains showed a near-wild type phenotype (Figure 6E). Results were similar with a dRictor null allele and a dSin1dsRNA (data not shown). dSin1-/- and dRictor-/- mutants display reduced Akt-dependent phosphorylation and inactivation of dFoxO [49], the single Drosophila ortholog of FoxO transcription factors. This suggests that TORC2 loss might antagonize glial neoplasia through dFoxO upregulation. However, excess dFoxOSA, which is resistant to dAkt phosphorylation [45], only partially suppressed repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glial overproliferation (Figure 6F), arguing that TORC2 has additional roles. Notably, on their own, dSin1-/- and dRictor-/- mutant flies did not show any detectable glial defects (Figure 6G, data not shown). Thus, TORC2 is dispensible for normal glial development, but is necessary for dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glial neoplasia.
###end p 46
###begin p 47
###xml 199 203 199 203 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Guertin1">[47]</xref>
###xml 451 461 451 461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 584 590 584 585 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 596 600 591 595 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 672 683 667 678 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g006">Figure 6I&#8211;K</xref>
###xml 688 698 683 693 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s010">Figure S10</xref>
###xml 802 811 797 806 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g006">Figure 6L</xref>
###xml 862 868 857 858 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 874 878 864 868 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 852 878 847 868 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 897 906 887 896 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g006">Figure 6H</xref>
###xml 941 946 931 936 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 975 978 965 968 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">act</sup>
###xml 1095 1105 1085 1095 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s010">Figure S10</xref>
###xml 1123 1127 1113 1117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Guertin1">[47]</xref>
###xml 1128 1132 1118 1122 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Teleman1">[49]</xref>
###xml 1262 1265 1252 1255 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">act</sup>
###xml 1323 1329 1313 1314 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
TORC1, a complex including Tor and the Raptor regulatory protein, drives cellular growth by stimulating protein synthesis through its effectors S6 kinase and the eIF-4E translation initiation factor [47]. Akt and Erk stimulate TORC1 through phosphorylation and inactivation of the TSC1-TSC2 protein complex, which activates Rheb, and stimulates TORC1 kinase activity. We tested TORC1 function by glial-specific overexpression of dsRNAs for the single Drosophila orthologs of Raptor (dRaptor), S6-kinase (dS6K), and eIF4E (deIF4E); these all significantly reduced accumulation of dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX mutant glial cells, but only caused mild glial hypoplasia in controls (Figure 6I-K and Figure S10). Co-overexpression of d4EBP, a deIF4E antagonist and dFoxO target gene, also blocked glial neoplasia (Figure 6L). Glial-specific RNAi of dTSC1 enhanced repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glial overgrowth (Figure 6H). However, overexpression of dTSC1dsRNA, dRheb, activated dS6K (dS6Kact), or deIF4E alone did not produce glial overproliferation, even though these constructs can mimic TORC1 activation (Figure S10, data not shown) [47],[49]. Thus, TORC1 activity is necessary for EGFR-PI3K-driven glial neoplasia, but is not sufficient. Moreover, neither deIF4E nor dS6Kact produced glial neoplasia when co-overexpressed with dEGFRlambda (data not shown), illustrating that additional dTor-dependent outputs synergize with dEGFR signaling to drive neoplasia.
###end p 47
###begin title 48
Myc and Max Drive EGFR;PI3K Glial Neoplasia via CyclinD-Cdk4
###end title 48
###begin p 49
###xml 161 171 161 171 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 219 223 219 223 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Teleman1">[49]</xref>
###xml 344 348 344 348 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Teleman1">[49]</xref>
###xml 349 353 349 353 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Tapon1">[50]</xref>
###xml 444 448 444 448 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Prober1">[16]</xref>
###xml 449 453 449 453 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Pelengaris1">[51]</xref>
dTor coordinates increased translation, mediated by dS6K and deIF4E, with expression of cell cycle regulators and ribosomal components, through dMyc, the single Drosophila ortholog of the Myc bHLH transcription factors [49]. Within developing epithelial tissues, dMyc is required for TORC1-dependent growth and can substitute for dTor activity [49],[50]. Myc protein levels can also be posttranslationally upregulated by EGFR-Ras-Raf signaling [16],[51]. Thus, we suspected that dMyc might mediate signal integration between EGFR-Ras and PI3K.
###end p 49
###begin p 50
###xml 5 11 5 6 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 17 21 12 16 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 90 106 85 101 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g007">Figure 7A and 7B</xref>
###xml 166 175 161 170 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 241 245 236 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Betschinger1">[21]</xref>
###xml 268 272 263 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dMyc</italic>
###xml 347 353 342 343 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 359 363 349 353 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 381 390 371 380 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g007">Figure 7D</xref>
###xml 427 430 417 420 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 442 448 432 433 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 454 458 439 443 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 423 458 413 443 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dMyc<sup>+/&#8722;</sup>; repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia showed high levels of nuclear dMyc compared to wild-type glia (Figure 7A and 7B). dMyc was also highly expressed in wild-type neuroblasts (Figure 7A), suggesting that dMyc promotes a proliferative progenitor state [21]. Genetic reduction of dMyc with a dsRNA or a single loss-of-function allele strongly suppressed dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glial neoplasia (Figure 7D, data not shown). In fact, some dMyc+/-; repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX animals were rescued to viability, indicating that dMyc is an essential rate-limiting output of EGFR-PI3K coactivation.
###end p 50
###begin title 51
Myc and Max are required to drive EGFR;PI3K glial neoplasia via CyclinD-Cdk4.
###end title 51

###begin p 53
###xml 163 173 163 173 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 218 224 218 219 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 230 234 225 229 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 208 234 208 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 247 256 242 251 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g007">Figure 7E</xref>
###xml 388 392 383 387 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Orian1">[52]</xref>
###xml 442 448 437 438 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 454 458 444 448 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 432 458 427 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 488 493 478 483 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 495 506 485 496 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g007">Figure 7F&#8211;H</xref>
###xml 683 687 673 677 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Lee2">[23]</xref>
###xml 694 697 684 687 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 709 715 699 700 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 721 725 706 710 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 689 725 679 710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dCdk4<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>; repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 820 829 805 814 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g007">Figure 7I</xref>
###xml 849 854 834 839 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 867 872 852 857 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 894 900 879 880 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 906 910 886 890 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 884 910 869 890 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 1042 1051 1022 1031 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g007">Figure 7J</xref>
Myc proteins activate transcription through heterodimerization with the bHLH Max. Max activity was also required for glial neoplasia; a dsRNA for dMax, the single Drosophila Max ortholog, strongly suppressed repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX overgrowth (Figure 7E). dMyc-dMax heterodimers promote proliferation by activating expression of multiple cell cycle genes, including dCyclinD and dCdk4 [52]. dCyclinD expression, which is high in repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia, was inhibited by a dMycdsRNA (Figure 7F-H), suggesting that dMyc reduction suppresses glial neoplasia through reduced dCyclinD-dCdk4 activity. To test this we used loss-of-function mutations in dCdk4, which are viable [23]. dCdk4-/-; repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX larvae showed near complete absence of excess glia and rescue of glial morphogenesis defects (Figure 7I). Moreover, a dCdk4dsRNA and dCyclinDdsRNA suppressed repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX (data not shown). Thus, dCyclinD-dCdk4 is essential for EGFR-PI3K glial neoplasia, although dCdk4 is not required for development (Figure 7J).
###end p 53
###begin title 54
Myc Overexpression or Rb Loss Synergizes with EGFR
###end title 54
###begin p 55
###xml 87 96 87 96 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g008">Figure 8C</xref>
###xml 143 152 143 152 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g008">Figure 8C</xref>
###xml 348 354 348 349 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 406 412 401 402 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 418 422 408 412 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 396 422 391 412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 424 433 414 423 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g008">Figure 8D</xref>
dMyc is necessary for glial neoplasia, but is not sufficient when overexpressed alone (Figure 8C). dMyc-overexpressing glia showed polyploidy (Figure 8C, data not shown), indicating that these cells undergo DNA replication without mitosis, but require additional signals for cell cycle progression. In contrast, co-overexpression of dMyc with dEGFRlambda produced a phenotype on par with that of repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX (Figure 8D), indicating that dMyc overexpression can substitute for PI3K activation and promote neoplasia when combined with EGFR signaling.
###end p 55
###begin title 56
Myc overexpression or Rb loss synergizes with EGFR.

(A-G) 2 microm optical sections of larval brain hemispheres from late 3rd instar larvae, displayed at the same scale. 20 microm scale bars. Frontal sections, midway through brains. Anterior up; midline to left. Glial cell nuclei are labeled with Repo (red); glial cell bodies and membranes are labeled with CD8GFP (green) driven by repo-Gal4; HRP (blue) reveals neuropil at high intensity and neuronal cell bodies at low intensity. repo>dMyc brains (C) contain many glia with enlarged nuclei (arrows). repo>dEGFRlambda;dMyc (D) brains have excess glia (red) throughout the brain, and these glia have very compact cell bodies (green) relative to wild-type glia (B). repo>dEGFRlambda;dCyclinD;dCdk4 (E) and repo>dEGFRlambda;Rbf1dsRNA (F) brains display increased numbers of glia (red) relative to wild-type (B), but show a less severe glial phenotype and a more normal neuronal compartment (blue) than either repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX (A) or repo>dEGFRlambda;dMyc (D). The combination of repo>Rbf1dsRNA;dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX (G) enhances neoplasia, leading to a dramatic increase in aberrant glia. (H,I) dCyclinE expression (red) in repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia (H) and in repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX;Rbf1dsRNA glia (I), alone and overlaid with the Repo glial marker (blue, right panels). dCyclinE is more strongly and more broadly expressed in neoplastic glia upon Rbf1 loss, as evidenced by the increased number and intensity of dCyclinE-expressing glial nuclei in (I) compared to (H). Anterior is up, midline to the left. 4.5 microm optical projections; 20 microm scale bars. (J) Pathway diagram of key effectors involved in glial neoplasia initiated by EGFR and PI3K, showing the pathway circuits driving cell cycle entry and progression, and protein translation. Arrows indicate pathway connections, although these connections are not necessarily direct. Genotypes: (A) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (B) repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (C) UAS-dMyc/repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP, (D) UAS-dEGFRlambda/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-dMyc, (E) UAS-dEGFRlambda/+; UAS-dCyclinD UAS-dCdk4/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP, (F) UAS-dEGFRlambda/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-Rbf1dsRNA, (G) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-Rbf1dsRNA, (H) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/+, (I) UAS-dEGFRlambda UAS-dp110CAAX/+; repo-Gal4 UAS-CD8GFP/UAS-Rbf1dsRNA.

###begin p 58
###xml 65 71 65 66 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 77 81 72 76 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 167 173 162 163 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 272 276 262 266 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Lee2">[23]</xref>
###xml 303 309 293 294 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 278 309 268 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dCyclinD;dCdk4;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup></italic>
###xml 323 328 308 313 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsRNA</sup>
###xml 334 340 319 320 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 314 340 299 320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;Rbf1<sup>dsRNA</sup>;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup></italic>
###xml 424 430 404 405 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 436 440 411 415 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 414 440 394 415 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repo&gt;dEGFR<sup>&#955;</sup>;dp110<sup>CAAX</sup></italic>
###xml 450 466 425 441 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g008">Figure 8E and 8F</xref>
###xml 697 701 672 676 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Teleman1">[49]</xref>
###xml 702 706 677 681 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000374-Orian1">[52]</xref>
###xml 757 763 732 733 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#955;</sup>
###xml 769 773 739 743 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAAX</sup>
###xml 807 815 777 785 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000374-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 820 830 790 800 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000374.s011">Figure S11</xref>
Given that the dMyc targets dCyclinD-dCdk4 are required for dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX neoplasia, we tested whether dCyclinD-dCdk4 overexpression could cooperate with dEGFRlambda. Additionally, we tested loss of Rbf1, the only known dCdk4 substrate that controls proliferation [23]. repo>dCyclinD;dCdk4;dEGFRlambda and repo>Rbf1dsRNA;dEGFRlambda animals showed glial overgrowth, but did not accumulate as many cells as repo>dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX animals (Figure 8E and 8F). Thus, glia likely require additional dp110 or dMyc effectors to undergo full neoplastic proliferation. Other known PI3K and dMyc-dMax target genes that promote proliferation include ribosomal proteins and translation regulators [49],[52], such as eIF4E, which is highly expressed in dEGFRlambda;dp110CAAX glia and required for neoplasia (Figure 6 and Figure S11).
###end p 58
